<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2><p>
Twain was born Eilleen Regina Edwards in <a href="/wiki/Windsor,_Ontario" title="Windsor, Ontario">Windsor, Ontario</a>, on August 28, 1965,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> to Sharon (<i>née</i> Morrison) and Clarence Edwards. She has two sisters, Jill and Carrie Ann. Her parents divorced when she was two and her mother moved to <a href="/wiki/Timmins,_Ontario" class="mw-redirect" title="Timmins, Ontario">Timmins, Ontario</a>, with her daughters. Sharon married Jerry Twain, an <a href="/wiki/Ojibwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ojibwa">Ojibwa</a> from the nearby <a href="/wiki/Mattagami_First_Nation" title="Mattagami First Nation">Mattagami First Nation</a>, and they had son Mark together. Jerry adopted the girls and legally changed their surname to Twain. When Mark was a toddler, Jerry and Sharon adopted Jerry's baby nephew Darryl when his mother died. Because of Twain's connection to Jerry, the media have incorrectly reported that she is of Ojibwe descent.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> When questioned as to why she chose not to publicly acknowledge Edwards as her father for years, Twain stated: </p><blockquote><p>My father (Jerry) went out of his way to raise three daughters that weren't even his. For me to acknowledge another man as my father, a man who was never there for me a father, who wasn't the one who struggled everyday to put food on our table, would have hurt him terribly. We were a family. Step-father, step-brothers, we never used that vocabulary in our home. To have referred to him as my step-father would have been the worst slap across the face to him.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote><p>Shania currently holds a status card and is on the official band membership list of the <a href="/wiki/Temagami_First_Nation" title="Temagami First Nation">Temagami First Nation</a>. In 1991, the singer was offered a recording contract in Nashville and applied for immigration status into the United States. At that time, by virtue of her stepfather Jerry Twain being a full-blooded Ojibway and the rights guaranteed to Native Americans in the <a href="/wiki/Jay_Treaty" title="Jay Treaty">Jay Treaty</a> (1795), Shania became legally registered as having 50 per cent Native American blood.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Twain has said that as a child she was told by her mother that her biological father was part Cree, a claim his family denies.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Her confirmed ancestry includes English, French, and Irish.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Through a maternal great-grandmother, she is a descendant of French carpenter <a href="/wiki/Zacharie_Cloutier" title="Zacharie Cloutier">Zacharie Cloutier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_d_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_d-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Her Irish maternal grandmother, Eileen Pearce, emigrated from <a href="/wiki/Newbridge,_County_Kildare" title="Newbridge, County Kildare">Newbridge, County Kildare</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Twain has said she had a difficult childhood. Her parents earned little money and food was often scarce in their household. Twain did not confide her situation to school authorities, fearing they might break up the family. Her mother and stepfather's marriage was stormy at times, and from a young age she witnessed violence between them. Her mother also struggled with bouts of depression. In mid-1979, while Jerry was at work, at Twain's insistence, her mother drove the rest of the family 420 miles (680&#160;km) south to a <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a> homeless shelter for assistance.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_f_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_f-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Sharon returned to Jerry with the children in 1981. In Timmins, Twain started singing at bars at the age of eight to try to help pay her family's bills; she often earned <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">$</a>20 between midnight and 1 a.m. performing for remaining customers after the bar had finished serving alcohol. Although she expressed a dislike for singing in those bars, Twain believes that this was her own kind of performing-arts school on the road.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_h_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_h-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> She has said of the ordeal, "My deepest passion was music and it helped. There were moments when I thought, 'I hate this.' I hated going into bars and being with drunks. But I loved the music and so I survived."<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_i_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_i-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Twain wrote her first songs at the age of 10, "Is Love a Rose" and "Just Like the Storybooks," which were rhyming fairy tales.<sup id="cite_ref-Eggar_2005_p=51_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggar_2005_p=51-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> She states that the art of creating, of actually writing songs, "was very different from performing them and became progressively important".<sup id="cite_ref-Eggar_2005_p=51_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggar_2005_p=51-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At age 13, Twain was invited to perform on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Canadian Broadcasting Corporation">CBC</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Tommy_Hunter" title="Tommy Hunter">Tommy Hunter</a> Show</i>. While attending <a href="/wiki/Timmins_High_and_Vocational_School" title="Timmins High and Vocational School">Timmins High and Vocational School</a>, she was also the singer for a local band called Longshot, which covered Top 40 music.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In the early 1980s, Twain spent some time working with her father's <a href="/wiki/Reforestation" title="Reforestation">reforestation</a> business in northern Ontario, which employed some 75 Ojibwe and Cree workers. Although the work was demanding and the pay low, Twain said, "I loved the feeling of being stranded. I'm not afraid of being in my own environment, being physical, working hard. I was very strong, I walked miles and miles every day and carried heavy loads of trees. You can't shampoo, use soap or deodorant, or makeup, nothing with any scent; you have to bathe and rinse your clothes in the lake. It was a very rugged existence, but I was very creative and I would sit alone in the forest with my dog and a guitar and would just write songs."<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_j_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_j-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="1983.E2.80.931992:_Beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1983–1992:_Beginnings">1983–1992: Beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1983–1992: Beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kenogami_Lake_ON.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Kenogami_Lake_ON.JPG/220px-Kenogami_Lake_ON.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Kenogami_Lake_ON.JPG/330px-Kenogami_Lake_ON.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Kenogami_Lake_ON.JPG/440px-Kenogami_Lake_ON.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1156" data-file-height="757" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kenogami_Lake_ON.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kenogami_Lake,_Ontario" title="Kenogami Lake, Ontario">Kenogami Lake, Ontario</a> where Twain spent much time practicing in 1985</div></div></div>
<p>Twain graduated from Timmins High in June 1983 eager to expand her musical horizons.<sup id="cite_ref-Eggy_2005_p=88_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggy_2005_p=88-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> After Longshot's demise, Twain was approached by a cover band led by <a href="/wiki/Diane_Chase" title="Diane Chase">Diane Chase</a> called "Flirt" and toured all over Ontario with them.<sup id="cite_ref-Eggy_2005_p=88_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggy_2005_p=88-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> She also took singing lessons from Toronto-based coach Ian Garrett, often cleaning his house as payment.<sup id="cite_ref-Eggar_2005_p=89_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggar_2005_p=89-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In the autumn of 1984, Twain's talents were noticed by Toronto DJ Stan Campbell who wrote about her in a <i>Country Music News</i> article: "Eilleen possesses a powerful voice with an impressive range. She has the necessary drive, ambition and positive attitude to achieve her goals".<sup id="cite_ref-Eggar_2005_p=89_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggar_2005_p=89-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Campbell happened to be making an album by Canadian musician (and present-day <a href="/wiki/CKTB_(AM)" class="mw-redirect" title="CKTB (AM)">CKTB</a> radio personality) Tim Denis at the time and Twain was featured on the backing vocals of the song <i>Heavy on the Sunshine</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_k_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_k-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Eggar_2005_p=89_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggar_2005_p=89-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Campbell later took Twain to Nashville to record some demos, which she found particularly difficult to finance. She became acquainted with regional country singer Mary Bailey who had had some country chart success in 1976. Bailey had seen Twain perform in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Sudbury" title="Greater Sudbury">Sudbury</a>, Ontario, saying "I saw this little girl up on stage with a guitar and it absolutely blew me away. She performed <a href="/wiki/Willie_Nelson" title="Willie Nelson">Willie Nelson</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Blue_Eyes_Crying_in_the_Rain" title="Blue Eyes Crying in the Rain">Blue Eyes Crying in the Rain</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Hank_Williams" title="Hank Williams">Hank Williams</a>' "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_So_Lonesome_I_Could_Cry" title="I&#39;m So Lonesome I Could Cry">I'm So Lonesome I Could Cry</a>". Her voice reminded me of <a href="/wiki/Tanya_Tucker" title="Tanya Tucker">Tanya Tucker</a>, it had strength and character, a lot of feeling. She's a star, she deserves an opportunity."<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_l_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_l-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Bailey later said "She sang a few songs that she had written, and I thought to myself, this kid is like nineteen years old, where does she get this? This is from a person who's lived sixty years".<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_m_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_m-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bailey acquired the contract from Stan Campbell and Twain moved into Bailey's home on <a href="/wiki/Kenogami_Lake,_Ontario" title="Kenogami Lake, Ontario">Kenogami Lake</a> where she practised her music every day for hours. In the fall of 1985, Bailey took Twain down to <a href="/wiki/Nashville" class="mw-redirect" title="Nashville">Nashville</a> to stay with a friend, record producer Tony Migliore, who at the time was producing an album for fellow Canadian singer Kelita Haverland and Twain was featured on the backing vocals to the song <i>Too Hot to Handle</i>. She also recorded "demo" songs with Cyril Rawson but those efforts were unsuccessful, partly due to Twain's wish to become a rock singer, not a country artist. After five months she returned to Canada and moved in with Bailey in a flat in downtown <a href="/wiki/Kirkland_Lake" title="Kirkland Lake">Kirkland Lake</a>, not far from Kenogami.<sup id="cite_ref-Eggar_2005_p=92_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggar_2005_p=92-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
There she met rock keyboardist Eric Lambier, drummer Randy Yurko, guitarist Tom Gustar and formed a new band, moving three months later to <a href="/wiki/Bowmanville" title="Bowmanville">Bowmanville</a>, near Toronto. In late summer 1986, Mary Bailey arranged for Twain to meet <a href="/wiki/John_Kim_Bell" title="John Kim Bell">John Kim Bell</a>, a half <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Mohawk nation">Mohawk</a>, half American conductor who had close contacts with the directors of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Country_Music_Association" title="Canadian Country Music Association">Canadian Country Music Association</a>. Bell recognized Twain's ability as well as her looks and the two began secretly dating.<sup id="cite_ref-Eggar_2005_p=92_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggar_2005_p=92-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In the fall of 1986 Twain continued to express her desire to be a pop or rock singer rather than country, which led to her falling out with Mary Bailey for two years. Twain's first break finally came on February 8, 1987, when Bell staged a fundraiser for the <a href="/wiki/Indspire" title="Indspire">National Aboriginal Achievement Foundation</a>, now Indspire, at the <a href="/wiki/Roy_Thomson_Hall" title="Roy Thomson Hall">Roy Thomson Hall</a> in Toronto where Twain performed with Broadway star <a href="/wiki/Bernadette_Peters" title="Bernadette Peters">Bernadette Peters</a>, jazz guitarist <a href="/wiki/Don_Ross_(guitarist)" title="Don Ross (guitarist)">Don Ross</a>, and the Toronto Symphony Orchestra. Her performance received little acclaim, but it convinced Bell, who hated pop music, that Twain should stay well away from it and concentrate on country music.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_n_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_n-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On November 1, 1987, Twain's mother and stepfather died in a car accident approximately 50 kilometres north of <a href="/wiki/Wawa,_Ontario" title="Wawa, Ontario">Wawa, Ontario</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_o_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_o-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> She moved back to Timmins to take care of her younger siblings and took them all to <a href="/wiki/Huntsville,_Ontario" title="Huntsville, Ontario">Huntsville, Ontario</a>, where she supported them by earning money performing at the nearby <a href="/wiki/Deerhurst_Resort" title="Deerhurst Resort">Deerhurst Resort</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eggar2005_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggar2005-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1993.E2.80.931994:_Shania_Twain"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1993–1994:_Shania_Twain">1993–1994: <i>Shania Twain</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1993–1994: Shania Twain">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several years later, when Twain's siblings moved out on their own, she assembled a demo tape of her songs and her Huntsville manager set up a showcase for her to present her material to record executives. She caught the attention of a few labels, including <a href="/wiki/Mercury_Nashville_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercury Nashville Records">Mercury Nashville Records</a>, who signed her within a few months.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> During this time, she changed her name to Shania, which was said to be an <a href="/wiki/Ojibwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ojibwa">Ojibwa</a> word which means "on my way." However, Twain's biographer, Robin Eggar, writes: "There is a continuing confusion about what 'Shania' means and if indeed it is an Ojibwe word or phrase at all. [...] There is no mispronounced or misheard phrase in either Ojibwe or Cree that comes close to meaning 'on my way.' Yet the legend of her name continues to be repeated in the media to this day."<sup id="cite_ref-Eggar_2005_p=145_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eggar_2005_p=145-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Eggar was mistaken about there being no Ojibwe phrase that "comes close", as "Ani aya'aa", pronounced "Ah-nih Eye-uh-ah", means "someone on the way" in Ojibwe. It is therefore possible that someone with an imperfect knowledge of the Ojibwe language created Shania with the incorrect idea it would mean "she's on the way".<sup id="cite_ref-Evans_2018_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Evans_2018-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Twain's <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain_(album)" title="Shania Twain (album)">self-titled debut album</a> was released in 1993 in North America and garnered her audiences outside Canada. Shortly before its release, she sang backing vocals for other Mercury artists, including <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Chance" title="Jeff Chance">Jeff Chance</a>'s 1992 album <i>Walk Softly on the Bridges</i><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sammy_Kershaw" title="Sammy Kershaw">Sammy Kershaw</a>'s 1993 album <i><a href="/wiki/Haunted_Heart_(Sammy_Kershaw_album)" title="Haunted Heart (Sammy Kershaw album)">Haunted Heart</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> While <i>Shania Twain</i> only reached No. 67 on the US Country Albums Chart, it gained positive reviews from critics. The album failed to sell significant copies initially. However, Twain's future success generated enough interest for the album to be certified platinum six years later by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), denoting sales of over 1 million. The album yielded two minor hit singles in the United States with "<a href="/wiki/What_Made_You_Say_That" title="What Made You Say That">What Made You Say That</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Dance_with_the_One_That_Brought_You" title="Dance with the One That Brought You">Dance with the One That Brought You</a>". The album was more successful in Europe, where Twain won Country Music Television Europe's "Rising Video Star of the Year" award.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In her 2011 autobiography <i>From This Moment On</i>, Twain expressed displeasure with her debut studio album, revealing that she had very little creative control and expressed frustration with not being able to showcase her songwriting ability.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1995.E2.80.931996:_The_Woman_in_Me_and_commercial_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1995–1996:_The_Woman_in_Me_and_commercial_success">1995–1996: <i>The Woman in Me</i> and commercial success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1995–1996: The Woman in Me and commercial success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When rock producer <a href="/wiki/Robert_John_%22Mutt%22_Lange" title="Robert John &quot;Mutt&quot; Lange">Robert John "Mutt" Lange</a> heard Twain's original songs and singing from her debut album, he offered to produce and write songs with her. After many telephone conversations, they met at <a href="/wiki/CMA_Music_Festival" title="CMA Music Festival">Nashville's Fan Fair</a> in June 1993. Twain and Lange became very close within just weeks, culminating in their wedding on December 28, 1993. Lange and Twain either wrote or co-wrote the songs that would form her second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Woman_in_Me_(Shania_Twain_album)" title="The Woman in Me (Shania Twain album)">The Woman in Me</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>The Woman in Me</i> was released on February 7, 1995. The album's first single, "<a href="/wiki/Whose_Bed_Have_Your_Boots_Been_Under%3F" title="Whose Bed Have Your Boots Been Under?">Whose Bed Have Your Boots Been Under?</a>" went to No. 11 on the <a href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs" title="Hot Country Songs"><i>Billboard</i> Country Chart</a>. This was followed by her first Country Top 10 and No.1 hit single, "<a href="/wiki/Any_Man_of_Mine" title="Any Man of Mine">Any Man of Mine</a>", which also cracked the Top 40 on the Billboard Hot 100. Twain had further hits from the album, including the title track which peaked at No.14 and three additional No.1 hits: "<a href="/wiki/(If_You%27re_Not_in_It_for_Love)_I%27m_Outta_Here!" title="(If You&#39;re Not in It for Love) I&#39;m Outta Here!">(If You're Not in It for Love) I'm Outta Here!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/You_Win_My_Love" title="You Win My Love">You Win My Love</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/No_One_Needs_to_Know" title="No One Needs to Know">No One Needs to Know</a>", which was selected for the original soundtrack for the 1996 film <i><a href="/wiki/Twister_(1996_film)" title="Twister (1996 film)">Twister</a></i>, a first for Twain, plus minor country hit "<a href="/wiki/Home_Ain%27t_where_His_Heart_Is_(Anymore)" title="Home Ain&#39;t where His Heart Is (Anymore)">Home Ain't where His Heart Is (Anymore)</a>" and a re-recorded gospel version of the album track "<a href="/wiki/God_Bless_the_Child_(Shania_Twain_song)" title="God Bless the Child (Shania Twain song)">God Bless The Child</a>" with new lyrics.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_38-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, in Australia, five of these singles: "Any Man of Mine", "The Woman in Me", "I'm Outta Here!" "You Win My Love" and "God Bless The Child," were remixed for the Australian pop market, and "I'm Outta Here!" became Twain's breakthrough hit there, reaching No.5 on the ARIA charts.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>As of 2007, the album had sold more than 12 million copies.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The album was a quick breakthrough and because of this Twain performed selected international venues and television shows including two CMA Fan Fair performances with Nashville guitarists <a href="/wiki/Randy_Thomas_(musician)" title="Randy Thomas (musician)">Randy Thomas</a> (co-writer of the song "<a href="/wiki/Butterfly_Kisses_(song)" title="Butterfly Kisses (song)">Butterfly Kisses</a>"), <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Joseph_Schafer" title="Daniel Joseph Schafer">Dan Schafer</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chris_Rodriguez" title="Chris Rodriguez">Chris Rodriguez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russ_Taff" title="Russ Taff">Russ Taff</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hugh_McDonald_(American_musician)" title="Hugh McDonald (American musician)">Hugh McDonald</a> bass player of <a href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi" title="Bon Jovi">Bon Jovi</a>, Dave Malachowski and Stanley T., formerly with <a href="/wiki/The_Beach_Boys" title="The Beach Boys">The Beach Boys</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Mercury Nashville's promotion of the album was based largely upon a series of music videos.<sup id="cite_ref-book544_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-book544-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> During this period, Twain made major television appearances on shows such as two performances on <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">Late Show with David Letterman</a></i>, <i>Blockbuster Music Awards</i>, <i>Billboard Music Awards</i> and the <i>American Music Awards</i>. <i>The Woman in Me</i> won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Country_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Country Album">Grammy Award for Best Country Album</a><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> award for Album of the Year;<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> the latter group also awarded Twain as Best New Female Vocalist.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1997.E2.80.932001:_Come_On_Over_and_international_pop_breakthrough"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1997–2001:_Come_On_Over_and_international_pop_breakthrough">1997–2001: <i>Come On Over</i> and international pop breakthrough</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1997–2001: Come On Over and international pop breakthrough">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shania_Twain_-_Come_on_Over_Tour_-_Boston.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Shania_Twain_-_Come_on_Over_Tour_-_Boston.jpg/220px-Shania_Twain_-_Come_on_Over_Tour_-_Boston.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Shania_Twain_-_Come_on_Over_Tour_-_Boston.jpg/330px-Shania_Twain_-_Come_on_Over_Tour_-_Boston.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Shania_Twain_-_Come_on_Over_Tour_-_Boston.jpg/440px-Shania_Twain_-_Come_on_Over_Tour_-_Boston.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="1035" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shania_Twain_-_Come_on_Over_Tour_-_Boston.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Twain performing on the <a href="/wiki/Come_On_Over_Tour" title="Come On Over Tour">Come On Over Tour</a> in 1999</div></div></div>
<p>In 1997, Twain released her follow-up album, <i><a href="/wiki/Come_On_Over" title="Come On Over">Come On Over</a></i>. This was the album that would establish her as a successful crossover singer. Slowly, following the release of lead singles <a href="/wiki/Love_Gets_Me_Every_Time" title="Love Gets Me Every Time">Love Gets Me Every Time</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Be_Stupid_(You_Know_I_Love_You)" title="Don&#39;t Be Stupid (You Know I Love You)">Don't Be Stupid (You Know I Love You)</a>", which allowed Twain to make more appearances in the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, the album started racking up sales. It never hit the top spot, but with the multi-chart hit single "<a href="/wiki/You%27re_Still_the_One" title="You&#39;re Still the One">You're Still the One</a>", sales skyrocketed. Other songs like "<a href="/wiki/When_(Shania_Twain_song)" title="When (Shania Twain song)">When</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Honey,_I%27m_Home" title="Honey, I&#39;m Home">Honey, I'm Home</a>", "<a href="/wiki/You%27ve_Got_a_Way" title="You&#39;ve Got a Way">You've Got a Way</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Man!_I_Feel_Like_a_Woman!" title="Man! I Feel Like a Woman!">Man! I Feel Like a Woman!</a>", "<a href="/wiki/That_Don%27t_Impress_Me_Much" title="That Don&#39;t Impress Me Much">That Don't Impress Me Much</a>", "<a href="/wiki/From_This_Moment_On_(Shania_Twain_song)" title="From This Moment On (Shania Twain song)">From This Moment On</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Rock_This_Country!" title="Rock This Country!">Rock This Country!</a>" and the title track are 8 of the 12 songs that eventually saw release as singles. "From This Moment On" is a duet with singer <a href="/wiki/Bryan_White" title="Bryan White">Bryan White</a> and there was a re-recorded solo pop version as well.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album stayed on the charts for the next two years, going on to sell 40 million copies worldwide, making it the biggest-selling album of all time by a female musician.<sup id="cite_ref-Harris2005_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harris2005-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> She continued to break international boundaries for country music and female crossover artists. It is also the eighth biggest-selling album by any type of artist in the US<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and the top selling country album in history. Songs from the album won four Grammy Awards during this time, including <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Country_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Country Song">Best Country Song</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Country_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Country Vocal Performance">Best Female Country Performance</a> (for "You're Still the One" and "Man! I Feel Like a Woman!") for Twain. Lange won Grammys for "You're Still the One" and "<a href="/wiki/Come_On_Over_(Shania_Twain_song)" title="Come On Over (Shania Twain song)">Come On Over</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite the album's record sales it wasn't able to top the <i>Billboard</i> 200, peaking at No.&#160;2. In 1998, following the pop release of "You're Still the One", the <i>Come On Over</i> album was released in a remixed format for the European market as a pop album with less country instrumentation, and actually gave her the big breakthrough in Europe she and her producer husband Robert John "Mutt" Lange were looking for. <i>Come On Over</i> went to No. 1 on the UK album charts for 11 weeks. It became the biggest selling album of the year in Great Britain and a bestseller in other big European markets as well, selling more than one million copies in Germany and nearly 4 million in the UK alone. Although "You're Still The One" and the pop version of "From This Moment On" cracked the Top 10 of the UK charts and "When" had minor success in the Top 20, the songs that had finally drawn European attention to the album were the pop remixed singles "That Don't Impress Me Much", a No.3 in the UK and Top 10 hit in Germany in the summer of 1999, and "Man! I Feel Like a Woman!" which peaked at No.3 in both the UK and France in autumn of that year. Additionally, "You've Got a Way" was remixed specifically for inclusion on the <i><a href="/wiki/Notting_Hill_(film)" title="Notting Hill (film)">Notting Hill</a></i> soundtrack. Subsequently, a reissue of the international version of the album was released worldwide, including the US and Europe, containing three of these new remixes. Additionally, the album set the record for the longest ever stay in the Top 20 of the <i>Billboard</i> 200, remaining in the Top 20 for 99 weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1998, Twain launched her first major concert tour, aided by her manager <a href="/wiki/Jon_Landau" title="Jon Landau">Jon Landau</a>, a veteran of many large-scale tours with <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Come_On_Over_Tour" title="Come On Over Tour">Come On Over Tour</a> shows were a success, winning the "Country Tour of the Year" in 1998 and 1999 by Pollstar Concert Industry Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2000, Twain was initially scheduled to release a Christmas album, but plans to release one were cancelled later in the year.<sup id="cite_ref-Brunner2000_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brunner2000-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following the success of <i>Come On Over</i>, independent label Limelight Records released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Complete_Limelight_Sessions" title="The Complete Limelight Sessions">The Complete Limelight Sessions</a></i> in October 2001. The album includes 16 tracks recorded in the late 1980s before Twain signed her record deal with Mercury.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2002.E2.80.932004:_Up.21"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2002–2004:_Up!">2002–2004: <i>Up!</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2002–2004: Up!">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After a change in management – QPrime replaced Landau&#160;– and a two-year break, along with the birth of their son, Eja (pronounced "Asia") D'Angelo, who was born on August 12, 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Twain and Lange returned to the studio. <i><a href="/wiki/Up!_(album)" title="Up! (album)">Up!</a></i> was released on November 19, 2002. On January 26, 2003, Twain performed at the Super Bowl halftime show. About a year later, Twain kicked off the <a href="/wiki/Up!_Tour" title="Up! Tour">Up! Tour</a> in <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton</a>, Ontario, Canada on September 25, 2003. <i>Up!</i> was released with three different discs – country/acoustic (green CD), pop/rock (red CD), and world/dance (blue CD). <i>Up!</i> was given four out of five stars by <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine, and debuted at No.1 on the <i>Billboard</i> albums chart, selling 874,000 in the first week alone. It remained at the top of the charts for five weeks. Twain's crossover appeal in country, pop, and dance music, led the album <i>Up!</i> to sell over 11 million copies by 2004. <i>Up!</i> reached No.1 in Germany, No.2 in Australia and the Top Five in the UK and France. In Germany, <i>Up!</i> was certified 4x platinum and stayed in the Top 100 for one and a half years. The international music disc was remixed with Indian-style orchestral and percussion parts recorded in <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>, India. The new versions were produced by Simon and <a href="/wiki/Diamond_Duggal" title="Diamond Duggal">Diamond Duggal</a>, brothers from <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a>, England. They were originally invited to contribute parts to the pop version of "I'm Gonna Getcha Good!" which retained the Indian influence.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_p_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_p-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ShaniaTwain3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ShaniaTwain3.jpg/220px-ShaniaTwain3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/ShaniaTwain3.jpg/330px-ShaniaTwain3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5d/ShaniaTwain3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="368" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ShaniaTwain3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Shania Twain performing during her <a href="/wiki/Up!_Tour" title="Up! Tour">Up! Tour</a> in 2004</div></div></div><p>Twain's popularity in UK was reflected by numerous appearances on the long-running music show <i><a href="/wiki/Top_of_the_Pops" title="Top of the Pops">Top of the Pops</a></i>, performing singles from <i>Come On Over</i> from 1999. In 2002 an entire special show was dedicated to her on sister show <i><a href="/wiki/TOTP2" class="mw-redirect" title="TOTP2">TOTP2</a></i>, in which Twain herself introduced some past performances of her greatest hits and new singles from <i>Up!</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-totp2_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-totp2-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> In November 2004, she appeared on the annual BBC charity telethon <i><a href="/wiki/Children_in_Need" title="Children in Need">Children in Need</a></i>. During the show, she performed "<a href="/wiki/Up!_(Shania_Twain_song)" title="Up! (Shania Twain song)">Up!</a>", and then took part in an all-star magic act in which she was sawn in half by magician Scott Penrose in an illusion called <a href="/wiki/Clearly_Impossible" title="Clearly Impossible">Clearly Impossible</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-walkoffame_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walkoffame-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first single from the album, "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Gonna_Getcha_Good!" title="I&#39;m Gonna Getcha Good!">I'm Gonna Getcha Good!</a>" became a top 10 country hit in the US, after debuting at No.&#160;24 after only five days of airplay; but only made the Top 40 on the pop charts. It was a much bigger hit on the other side of the Atlantic, released in a pop version, the single hit No. 4 in the UK. In Australia, Germany and France the song reached the Top 15 in each case. The follow-up single, "<a href="/wiki/Up!_(Shania_Twain_song)" title="Up! (Shania Twain song)">Up!</a>", reached the Top 15 in the US country charts but failed to reach the pop Top 40. The second European single became the mid-tempo song "<a href="/wiki/Ka-Ching!" title="Ka-Ching!">Ka-Ching!</a>" (which was never released as a single in North America) with lyrics where Twain was criticizing unchecked consumerism. The song eventually became another smash hit in the important European markets, reaching No.1 in Germany and Austria and other European countries, the UK Top 10 and the Top 15 in France.
</p><p>The third single from the album would be the most successful in the US. The romantic ballad "<a href="/wiki/Forever_and_for_Always" title="Forever and for Always">Forever and for Always</a>" was released as a single in April 2003 and peaked at No.4 on the country chart and No.1 on the Adult Contemporary chart, and made as well the <i>Billboard</i> Top 20. Again success was even bigger on the other side of the Atlantic with "Forever and For Always" again reaching the Top 10 in both, the UK and Germany. Further singles were "<a href="/wiki/She%27s_Not_Just_a_Pretty_Face" title="She&#39;s Not Just a Pretty Face">She's Not Just a Pretty Face</a>", which was a country Top 10 hit, while the last US single, "<a href="/wiki/It_Only_Hurts_When_I%27m_Breathing" title="It Only Hurts When I&#39;m Breathing">It Only Hurts When I'm Breathing</a>", made the Top 20 on both Country and AC. Due to the enormous European success of <i>Up!</i> and its first three singles, two more singles were released in the second half of 2003 with up-tempo "<a href="/wiki/Thank_You_Baby" class="mw-redirect" title="Thank You Baby">Thank You Baby</a>" (No. 11 in the UK, Top 20 in Germany) and just before Christmas the romantic, acoustic ballad "When You Kiss Me," at least a minor hit in both territories. The title track "Up!" also saw a single release in a limited edition of European countries, such as Germany, in early 2004. In January 2008, <i>Up!</i> had sold 5.5&#160;million copies in the US and was certified by the RIAA as 11x platinum (the organization counts double albums as two units).<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2004.E2.80.932010:_Greatest_Hits_and_delay_of_new_album"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2004–2010:_Greatest_Hits_and_delay_of_new_album">2004–2010: <i>Greatest Hits</i> and delay of new album</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2004–2010: Greatest Hits and delay of new album">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2004, she released the <i><a href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits_(Shania_Twain_album)" title="Greatest Hits (Shania Twain album)">Greatest Hits</a></i> album, with three new tracks. As of 2012, it had sold over 4.15&#160;million copies in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The first single, the multi-format duet "<a href="/wiki/Party_for_Two" title="Party for Two">Party for Two</a>", made the country top ten with <a href="/wiki/Billy_Currington" title="Billy Currington">Billy Currington</a>, while the pop version with <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Ray" title="Sugar Ray">Sugar Ray</a> lead singer <a href="/wiki/Mark_McGrath" title="Mark McGrath">Mark McGrath</a> made top ten in the United Kingdom and Germany. The follow-up singles, "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t!" title="Don&#39;t!">Don't!</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/I_Ain%27t_No_Quitter" title="I Ain&#39;t No Quitter">I Ain't No Quitter</a>" did not fare as well. The former made Top 20 on Adult Contemporary, while the latter did not gain enough airplay to reach the Country Top 40.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_1965_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_1965-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2005, she released the single "<a href="/wiki/Shoes_(Shania_Twain_song)" title="Shoes (Shania Twain song)">Shoes</a>" from the <i><a href="/wiki/Desperate_Housewives" title="Desperate Housewives">Desperate Housewives</a></i> soundtrack. In 2008, Twain and <a href="/wiki/Anne_Murray" title="Anne Murray">Anne Murray</a> recorded a duet version of Murray's hit "<a href="/wiki/You_Needed_Me" title="You Needed Me">You Needed Me</a>" for her 2007 album, <i><a href="/wiki/Anne_Murray_Duets:_Friends_%26_Legends" title="Anne Murray Duets: Friends &amp; Legends">Anne Murray Duets: Friends &amp; Legends</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2009, Twain released a letter to her fans explaining the delays in the release of her next album, noting she had gone through personal pains and was focusing on raising her son Eja.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_r_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_r-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In August 2009, at a conference in Timmins, Ontario, a spokesman for Twain's label said a new record from the singer was still "nowhere in sight".<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_s_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_s-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2011.E2.80.932015:_Return_to_music.2C_residency.2C_and_tour"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–2015:_Return_to_music,_residency,_and_tour">2011–2015: Return to music, residency, and tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2011–2015: Return to music, residency, and tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ShaniaTwainJune2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/ShaniaTwainJune2011.jpg/190px-ShaniaTwainJune2011.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="317" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/ShaniaTwainJune2011.jpg/285px-ShaniaTwainJune2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/ShaniaTwainJune2011.jpg/380px-ShaniaTwainJune2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="729" data-file-height="1216" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ShaniaTwainJune2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Twain announcing her upcoming <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Palace" title="Caesars Palace">Caesars Palace</a> show in Las Vegas in 2011</div></div></div>
<p>In May 2011, Twain confirmed in an interview that she would release her first new single in six years, "<a href="/wiki/Today_Is_Your_Day" title="Today Is Your Day">Today Is Your Day</a>", after the finale of <i><a href="/wiki/Why_Not%3F_with_Shania_Twain" title="Why Not? with Shania Twain">Why Not? with Shania Twain</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-today_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-today-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Twain previewed the song in the first episode of the series.<sup id="cite_ref-today_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-today-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Twain worked with music producers <a href="/wiki/David_Foster" title="David Foster">David Foster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Chapman_(record_producer)" title="Nathan Chapman (record producer)">Nathan Chapman</a> on the song. She also published her <a href="/wiki/Autobiography" title="Autobiography">autobiography</a> with <a href="/wiki/Atria_Publishing_Group" title="Atria Publishing Group">Atria Books</a>, <i>From This Moment On</i>. The last episode of "Why Not?" features Twain and <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Richie" title="Lionel Richie">Lionel Richie</a> recording "<a href="/wiki/Endless_Love_(song)" title="Endless Love (song)">Endless Love</a>" which would be the first single from his 2012 album, <i><a href="/wiki/Tuskegee_(album)" title="Tuskegee (album)">Tuskegee</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-cgm_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cgm-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> "Today Is Your Day" was officially released to iTunes and country radio on June 12, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-tcp_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcp-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> In addition to "Today Is Your Day", Twain also collaborated with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bubl%C3%A9" title="Michael Bublé">Michael Bublé</a> on his 2011 album <i><a href="/wiki/Christmas_(Michael_Bubl%C3%A9_album)" title="Christmas (Michael Bublé album)">Christmas</a></i> (also produced by David Foster). Twain recorded "<a href="/wiki/White_Christmas_(song)" title="White Christmas (song)">White Christmas</a>" with Bublé, which was the first single from the album.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On June 8, 2011, at a press conference at the <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Country Music Hall of Fame">Country Music Hall of Fame</a> in Nashville, Twain announced that she would headline <a href="/wiki/Caesars_Palace" title="Caesars Palace">Caesars Palace</a> in Las Vegas for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-tcp_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tcp-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> Her show, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Shania:_Still_the_One" title="Shania: Still the One">Still the One</a></i>, began on December 1, 2012, with shows expected to run in 2013 and 2014.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In July 2013, Twain announced on <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> that she was working on her album over the summer during a break from <i>Still the One</i>. In October 2013, Twain sat down with Robin Roberts from <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> as a featured artist on the Countdown to the CMA Awards. In the interview, Twain said that a new album was coming, but she said that she was still in the process of finding the right producer.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Outside of her show at Caesars Palace, Twain performed two concerts at the <a href="/wiki/Calgary_Stampede" title="Calgary Stampede">Calgary Stampede</a> in <a href="/wiki/Calgary,_Alberta" class="mw-redirect" title="Calgary, Alberta">Calgary, Alberta</a>, on July 9 and 10, 2014. In a series of interviews leading up to her Calgary Stampede shows, Twain said she hoped to tour in 2015 and that it would lead to the release of a new album.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Alongside her Calgary Stampede shows, Twain also headlined a show on Labour Day weekend at Charlottetown, Prince Edward Island, Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 4, 2015, Twain announced on <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i> she would be going on tour for the first time in 11 years, and would begin June 5 in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a>, Washington and end on October 11 in Toronto, Ontario. Twain also announced this would be her last tour before her fifth studio album, which she intends to release while she is 50.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> In an interview on Global Television Network's <i>The Morning Show</i> on March 6, Twain confirmed that she is not retiring from her music career after the tour.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In an interview with Radio.com published on March 5, she stated that she has found several producers for her upcoming album, describing it as "soul music".<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 24, 2015, Twain stated: "First, I have to finish my new album this winter. Six tracks are already completed. I've written 38 songs in total, and now the process is underway to narrow that down to another six or eight to finish recording". That same month, it was announced by several sources, that even though her current <a href="/wiki/Rock_This_Country_Tour" title="Rock This Country Tour">Rock This Country Tour</a> is her final time touring, she is possibly planning on extending the tour overseas because the Rock This Country tour was only based in the United States and Canada. Twain also mentioned, possibly returning to Las Vegas with a new residency show for possibly late 2016 or 2017. The new show would end up featuring music from her long-awaited new album as well as her hits.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2016.E2.80.93present:_Now.2C_second_Las_Vegas_residency"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–present:_Now,_second_Las_Vegas_residency">2016–present: <i>Now</i>, second Las Vegas residency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2016–present: Now, second Las Vegas residency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2016, Twain confirmed to <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> that she had new music coming "really soon."<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In December 2016 in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Billboard magazine">Billboard</a></i>, she spoke about her forthcoming album, describing the finished product as "kind of schizophrenic musically" maintaining "She's the glue".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In February 2017, Twain again spoke to <i>Rolling Stone</i> about the album; select song titles were confirmed, as Twain detailed that she had not only hoped to release a single in March, but that she planned to release the album in May.<sup id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_1_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_1-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> She performed at the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Festival" title="Stagecoach Festival">Stagecoach Festival</a>, held on April 29.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2017, <i>Billboard</i> announced that Twain's new single, "<a href="/wiki/Life%27s_About_to_Get_Good" title="Life&#39;s About to Get Good">Life's About to Get Good</a>", would premiere in June, with the album projected for release in September. Twain headlined the 2017 Stagecoach Festival in Indio, California, where she previewed her new music for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Twain performed on the <i><a href="/wiki/Today_(U.S._TV_program)" class="mw-redirect" title="Today (U.S. TV program)">Today Show</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s "Summer Concert Series" on June 16, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Her fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Now_(Shania_Twain_album)" title="Now (Shania Twain album)">Now</a>,</i> was released on September 29, 2017<sup id="cite_ref-Twain&#39;s_New_Single_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Twain&#39;s_New_Single-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> and would debut at No. 1 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2017, Twain announced on ET Canada that she would in fact tour with her new album <i>Now</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Now_Tour_(Shania_Twain_tour)" class="mw-redirect" title="Now Tour (Shania Twain tour)">Now Tour</a> was announced by Twain on her official website on August 17, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Tour_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tour-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The album's second single, "<a href="/wiki/Swingin%27_With_My_Eyes_Closed" class="mw-redirect" title="Swingin&#39; With My Eyes Closed">Swingin' With My Eyes Closed</a>", was released on August 18, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> She has also internationally released two other promotional singles off of <i>Now</i>, including "Poor Me" and "We've Got Something They Don't".<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2019, Twain announced her second Las Vegas residency, <i><a href="/wiki/Shania:_Let%27s_Go!" title="Shania: Let&#39;s Go!">Let's Go!</a></i>, opens December 2019, and will run for two years.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="TV_and_film_career">TV and film career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: TV and film career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Twain's mainstream pop acceptance was further helped by her appearance in the 1998 first edition of the <i><a href="/wiki/VH1_Divas" title="VH1 Divas">VH1 Divas</a></i> concert where she sang alongside <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celine_Dion" title="Celine Dion">Celine Dion</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gloria_Estefan" title="Gloria Estefan">Gloria Estefan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carole_King" title="Carole King">Carole King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aretha_Franklin" title="Aretha Franklin">Aretha Franklin</a>, and also by <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>'s 1999 heavily aired <i><a href="/wiki/Behind_the_Music" title="Behind the Music">Behind the Music</a></i>, which concentrated on the tragic aspects of her early life as well as her physical attractiveness and Nashville's early resistance to her bare-midriff music videos. After Divas, Shania Twain wrote and/or sang background vocals with her then husband Robert John "Mutt" Lange the songs, "<a href="/wiki/If_Walls_Could_Talk" title="If Walls Could Talk">If Walls Could Talk</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Goodbye%27s_(The_Saddest_Word)" title="Goodbye&#39;s (The Saddest Word)">Goodbye's (The Saddest Word)</a>" for Celine Dion.
</p><p>On November 12, 2008, Twain made her first television appearance since her split from ex-husband Robert "Mutt" Lange, where she appeared as a surprise presenter at the 42nd CMA Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_2008_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_2008-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2009, Twain served as a guest judge on <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i>, for the show's August 30 and 31 episodes.<sup id="cite_ref-AI_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AI-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2010, Twain announced plans for her own TV show, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Why_Not%3F_with_Shania_Twain" title="Why Not? with Shania Twain">Why Not? with Shania Twain</a></i>. The show debuted on May 8, 2011 on <a href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey_Network_(U.S._TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oprah Winfrey Network (U.S. TV channel)">OWN</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_u_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_u-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Twain returned to <i>American Idol</i> as a guest mentor for a week where the top 6 contestants showcased her songs.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_2010_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_2010-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> After the conclusion of the ninth season Twain was very close to becoming a judge but ultimately it was <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a> who got the job.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Twain guest starred on the <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">Comedy Central</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Broad_City" title="Broad City">Broad City</a></i>, in a September 2017 episode titled "Twaining Day".<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 23, 2017, Twain appeared as a guest judge on the 25th season of <i><a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars_(U.S._TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dancing with the Stars (U.S. TV series)">Dancing with the Stars</a></i> during the show's "Movie Night", and also performed her song "Soldier".<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Twain appeared as a guest judge on episode five of the 10th Season of <i><a href="/wiki/Rupaul%27s_Drag_Race" class="mw-redirect" title="Rupaul&#39;s Drag Race">Rupaul's Drag Race</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She competed against singer <a href="/wiki/Meghan_Trainor" title="Meghan Trainor">Meghan Trainor</a> in an episode of <a href="/wiki/TBS_(American_TV_channel)" title="TBS (American TV channel)">TBS</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Drop_the_Mic" title="Drop the Mic">Drop the Mic</a></i> which aired in January 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Twain was guest of honor for a <i><a href="/wiki/Lip_Sync_Battle" title="Lip Sync Battle">Lip Sync Battle</a></i> episode on <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Network" title="Paramount Network">Paramount Network</a> pitting <a href="/wiki/Derek_Hough" title="Derek Hough">Derek Hough</a> against <a href="/wiki/Nicole_Scherzinger" title="Nicole Scherzinger">Nicole Scherzinger</a> that was dedicated to her and her music. The tribute episode aired June 21, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In November 2018, Twain appeared in the reality talent show <i>Real Country</i>, as an executive producer and co-presenter with <a href="/wiki/Jake_Owen" title="Jake Owen">Jake Owen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Travis_Tritt" title="Travis Tritt">Travis Tritt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Twain will play the role of the mother of singer <a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Camp" title="Jeremy Camp">Jeremy Camp</a> in the 2020 <a href="/wiki/Biopic" class="mw-redirect" title="Biopic">biopic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/I_Still_Believe_(film)" title="I Still Believe (film)">I Still Believe</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Endorsements">Endorsements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Endorsements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In January 2005, Twain joined Scentstories by <a href="/wiki/Febreze" title="Febreze">Febreze</a> to create a limited edition scent disc with the proceeds going to <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Second_Harvest" class="mw-redirect" title="America&#39;s Second Harvest">America's Second Harvest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_w_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_w-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In late 2005, Twain partnered with <a href="/wiki/Coty,_Inc." title="Coty, Inc.">Coty</a> to produce her namesake fragrance "Shania" by Stetson. A second fragrance was released in September 2007, called "Shania Starlight".<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_x_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_x-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 1, 2010, Twain carried the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Flame" class="mw-redirect" title="Olympic Flame">Olympic Torch</a> through her hometown as part of the <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics_torch_relay" title="2010 Winter Olympics torch relay">2010 Winter Olympics torch relay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_t_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_t-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Twain is a vegetarian<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> and a devotee of <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_Sant_Mat_movements" title="Contemporary Sant Mat movements">Sant Mat</a>, an Eastern spiritual philosophy.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Twain met producer <a href="/wiki/Robert_John_%22Mutt%22_Lange" title="Robert John &quot;Mutt&quot; Lange">Robert John "Mutt" Lange</a> after he heard her original songs and singing from her debut album; he then offered to produce and write songs with her. They first met at <a href="/wiki/CMA_Music_Festival" title="CMA Music Festival">Nashville's Fan Fair</a> in June 1993 and quickly became close. They were married on December 28, 1993 and had a son, Eja (pronounced "Asia"), in August 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-peopleceleb_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-peopleceleb-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> On May 15, 2008, it was announced that Twain and Lange were separating after Lange allegedly had an affair with Twain's best friend, Marie-Anne Thiébaud.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_y_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_y-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ref_z_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_z-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Their divorce was finalized on June 9, 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-Julie2010_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Julie2010-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> On December 20, 2010, it was reported that Twain was engaged to Swiss <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a> executive Frédéric Thiébaud, the ex-husband of Marie-Anne.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> They were married on January 1, 2011, in <a href="/wiki/Rinc%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Rincón, Puerto Rico">Rincón, Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>She created Shania Kids Can in 2010, to address the needs of young school children who are typically overlooked by social assistance programs.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research#Primary,_secondary_and_tertiary_sources" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable secondary sources. (December 2018)">non-primary source needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Twain's autobiography, <i>From This Moment On</i>, was released on March 27, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Twain is a long-time resident of <a href="/wiki/Corseaux" title="Corseaux">Corseaux</a>, Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Her son was born there.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honours">Awards and honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Awards and honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Shania_Twain" title="List of awards and nominations received by Shania Twain">List of awards and nominations received by Shania Twain</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Shania_Twain_star_on_Walk_of_Fame.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Shania_Twain_star_on_Walk_of_Fame.jpg/220px-Shania_Twain_star_on_Walk_of_Fame.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Shania_Twain_star_on_Walk_of_Fame.jpg/330px-Shania_Twain_star_on_Walk_of_Fame.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Shania_Twain_star_on_Walk_of_Fame.jpg/440px-Shania_Twain_star_on_Walk_of_Fame.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2094" data-file-height="1679" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Shania_Twain_star_on_Walk_of_Fame.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Twain's star on <a href="/wiki/Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame" title="Canada&#39;s Walk of Fame">Canada's Walk of Fame</a></div></div></div>
<p>In addition to her various awards for her singles and albums, Twain has received a number of personal honours:
</p>
<ul><li>She was named the 1999 Entertainer of the Year by both the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association" title="Country Music Association">Country Music Association</a>; Twain was the first non-US citizen to win the CMA award.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li>Twain was ranked No.7 in <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Country Music Television">Country Music Television</a>'s <i>40 Greatest Women of Country Music</i> in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_ad_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_ad-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2003, Twain was inducted into <a href="/wiki/Canada%27s_Walk_of_Fame" title="Canada&#39;s Walk of Fame">Canada's Walk of Fame</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-walkoffame_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-walkoffame-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The city of Timmins <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, renamed a street for her, gave her the key to the city, and built the <a href="/wiki/Shania_Twain_Centre" title="Shania Twain Centre">Shania Twain Centre</a> in her honour.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_af_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_af-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On November 18, 2005, Twain was invested as an Officer in the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Canada" title="Order of Canada">Order of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_2005_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_2005-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ottawa2008_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ottawa2008-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Twain was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="Canadian Music Hall of Fame">Canadian Music Hall of Fame</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Juno_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Juno Awards">Juno Awards</a> on March 27, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>On June 2, 2011, Twain received a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>. Her star is the 2,442nd Star on the Hollywood Walk of Fame in the Category of Recording.<sup id="cite_ref-Ref_ae_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ref_ae-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2016, Twain was declared the "Artist of a Lifetime" by <a href="/wiki/CMT_(U.S._TV_channel)" class="mw-redirect" title="CMT (U.S. TV channel)">CMT</a> and was given a special award during the 2016 Artists of the Year ceremony.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In January 2017, it was announced that Twain will have her own exhibit at the <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum">Country Music Hall of Fame</a> titled <i>Shania Twain: Rock This Country</i>, which will open on June 26 and run through 2018.</li>
<li>In 2018, Twain was announced as the second recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Country_Music_Association" title="Canadian Country Music Association">CCMA</a> Generation Award.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> This is awarded to artists who have had significant impact in the country music industry as well as awareness of country music worldwide.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmography">Filmography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Filmography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/I_Heart_Huckabees" title="I Heart Huckabees">I Heart Huckabees</a></i> (2004) cameo<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Broad_City" title="Broad City">Broad City</a></i> (2017)<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Episode "Twaining Day"</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Trading_Paint" title="Trading Paint">Trading Paint</a></i> (2019)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/I_Still_Believe_(film)" title="I Still Believe (film)">I Still Believe</a></i> (2020)<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Concerts">Concerts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shania_Twain&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Concerts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>Co-headlining tours</b>
</p>
<ul><li>Triple Play Tour (1993; with <a href="/wiki/John_Brannen" title="John Brannen">John Brannen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toby_Keith" title="Toby Keith">Toby Keith</a>)</li></ul>
<p><b>Headlining tours</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Come_On_Over_Tour" title="Come On Over Tour">Come On Over Tour</a> (1998–1999)</li>
